import mysqlsh
import traceback

    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)

import json
import mysqlsh
import traceback

try:
    # Disable wizards in this script, since it will be invoked without --no-wizard
    shell.options.set('useWizards', False)
    import json

    cluster_set = dba.get_cluster_set()
    routers = cluster_set.list_routers()
    # mysqlsh objects are weirdâ€”they quack (i.e. duck typing) like standard Python objects (e.g. list,
    # dict), but do not serialize to JSON correctly.
    # Cast to str & load from JSON str before serializing
    routers = json.loads(str(routers))
    with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_output.json", "w") as file:
        json.dump(routers, file)
except mysqlsh.DBError as exception:
    error = {
        "message": str(exception),
        "code": exception.code,
        "traceback_message": "".join(traceback.format_exception(exception)),
    }
else:
    error = None
with open("/tmp/mysqlsh_error.json", "w") as file:
    json.dump(error, file)
